Um, you don't have to be an engineer to figure out why they are burning up.  It's simple, they are moving more power over fewer connections with smaller contacts featuring less surface area.  Impedance is a thing, and so is the heat created by it.  The same reason that the chonky 2.0 PCIe power connecters can only run 150 watts each 8 pins, any more and THEY catch fire because they would need more surface area to handle it.  So yeah, BRIGHT IDEA!  Let's run the power limit of 4 independent 8 pin high surface area connecters into 12 pins with a quarter of the surface area each, so it's like trying to run 600 watts through a single connector which can't handle more than 150 watts without catching fire...  And than wonder why they are catching fire.  I'm kinda surprised and shocked that they didn't respond to the complaints by calling it an added feature: A single use lighter.

@7.40 - The small logos on the fanblades actually reduces drag on the low pressure side by creating micro-turbulence near the surface. ( Like the hollow pattern on golfballs and "tooth patterns" on the "sharp" edge of helicopter rotors and large windturbines. ) Noctua also uses this technique on some of their fans. So If it works, who cares what it looks like. ;-)

I have never seen this leash system before. It's a great idea and I could definitely work with that in my server tower. Up top there is a pair of support bars that partition the power supply and top bezel from the mobo tray section and basically the rest of the guts of the computer. It has some small holes pre-drilled or punched for something that never shipped but it looks like it would work with this system. Pretty cool. I also like the BIOS switch LED. Probably a useful diagnostic lamp but even better that the main power connection was sent to the rear. It's pretty typical that when you have good designers, you have engineers that can keep up. Btw @JayzTwoCents if you gonna run and benchmark new gpu's i recommend doing that with a panel that is 10 bit color depth, AMD is having MPO related issues, and MPO is only enabled on primary monitor and at 8 bit color depth so 10 bit color depth should avoid all the MPO related issues, Nvidia had these issues as well, they have a page with reg files that can disable and enable MPO, i think a lot of MPO related issues still happen on Nvidia gpu's but the people that say it does not happen probably run 10 bit color depth, while those experiencing issues run 8 bit color depth, making MPO the biggest troll of all time.

0:47 Obama
Sooo, is anyone having trouble with their nVidia cards pegged near 100% at idle lately? You look and find 'dwm.exe' is the one pegging it, 'desktop window management'. Well, I and several others are having this problem and it seems to have been introduced sometime in the last two driver releases. The crazy part (or dumb part, depending on how you look at it) is that this isn't a 'new' bug. It's happened before and there are several Reddit threads about it from years ago and how to fix it.   If you have this problem, I suggest you take a look. There's two remedies, one being to rollback your driver to a version that doesn't bork it all up or to disable "Hardware-accelerated GPU scheduling" via Windows display graphics settings. I have no clue what that does or what I'm missing out on by disabling it but it worked for me! Now to wait until 1. nVidia admits they borked it and/or 2. releases a hotfix/new driver version with the fix. Something tells me I'm going to be waiting a while...
